The standard way is to express Kp in terms of \u03b1 and the total pressure, then solve for \u03b1. Here is a clear path and the core results you can use once Kp(T) is known:\\n\\n1) Let initial moles be n0 of N2O4 and no NO2. At equilibrium, with degree of dissociation \u03b1:\\n- n(N2O4) = n0(1 \u2212 \u03b1)\\n- n(NO2)  = 2 n0 \u03b1\\n- total n = n0(1 + \u03b1)\\n\\n2) Partial pressures (assuming total pressure P and using mole fractions):\\n- P_NO2 = [2\u03b1/(1 + \u03b1)] P\\n- P_N2O4 = [(1 \u2212 \u03b1)/(1 + \u03b1)] P\\n\\n3) The equilibrium constant in terms of partial pressures is\\nKp = (P_NO2)^2 / P_N2O4.\\nSubstitute the expressions from (2):\\nKp = [(2\u03b1/(1 + \u03b1))^2 P^2] / [(1 \u2212 \u03b1)/(1 + \u03b1) P]\\n= [4 \u03b1^2 P] / [(1 + \u03b1)(1 \u2212 \u03b1)]\\n= 4 \u03b1^2 P / (1 \u2212 \u03b1^2).\\nThis can be rearranged to give a neat closed form for \u03b1:\\nKp (1 \u2212 \u03b1^2) = 4 \u03b1^2 P  \u21d2  Kp = \u03b1^2 (Kp + 4P)  \u21d2  \u03b1^2 = Kp / (Kp + 4P).\\nThus\\n\u03b1 = sqrt[ Kp / (Kp + 4P) ],\\nwhere P is the total pressure (in the same units as the standard state for Kp, typically bar if Kp is taken with P\u00b0 = 1 bar).\\n\\n4) For your data: P = 1.50 bar, T = 300 K.
